### Post by MetalMusicAddict on 2007-01-08
Heres some of the new server I put together this year. I removed 2 5" and floppy drive bays to add more HD space. I have 8 now. The pics are a little old.

I also added a second front 120mm fan.

In the end this is WAY more power than my home server needs to be. My old 950mhz AMD went up (mobo actually) so when I got new cheap parts it was still alot of power.
If anyone wants to know the parts Ill edit this post.

The Ubuntu sticker came from the official .EPS. Its vinyl like car graffix. I worked at a sign shop so I made it and some more (smaller) to go on cars and laptops.
If you want to do this you can take the .EPS to any sign shop like "Fast Signs" or "Signs By Tomorrow" in the states and get 'em cut pretty cheap. 

 [[IMG]http://img98.imageshack.us/img98/3946/dscf21869nj.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img98.imageshack.us/my.php?image=dscf21869nj.jpg) [[IMG]http://img499.imageshack.us/img499/602/dscf21879gg.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img499.imageshack.us/my.php?image=dscf21879gg.jpg) [[IMG]http://img140.imageshack.us/img140/7875/dscf21891fz.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img140.imageshack.us/my.php?image=dscf21891fz.jpg) [[IMG]http://img140.imageshack.us/img140/1233/dscf21911az.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img140.imageshack.us/my.php?image=dscf21911az.jpg)

Bad light in my basement. My camera is also only at max iso600.

Oh, and as soon as a new kernel for debian stable gets released, that'll kill my uptime.  I've just been lucky that we haven't had any extended power outages or kernel updates to cause me to reboot.

### Post by RandomJoe on 2007-01-08
A pic of my server itself is pretty dull but some rather like the room as a whole - it isn't quite as impressive as it's been in the past, used to have 4 machines 24x7 which required the A/C run all the time.  (Have a mini-split unit mounted to the opposite wall.)  It's also a bit of a mess - really ought to tidy things up some day... :rolleyes: 

The three shots are a pan across the "interesting" walls.  I have everything in the walk-in closet of my office (back bedroom).  I mounted a few punchblocks that I scarfed from our old office as we moved out.  The top one is for the phone lines, the bottom two are LAN jacks I've installed in various places about the house.  I cut a hole in the ceiling and dropped a piece of pipe down from the attic to run the cable.

Gig-E switch, 100MB switch, Vonage, cablemodem, Slackware firewall box all sit on the upper shelf.  Dell PowerEdge server contains a 1TB RAID mostly for serving up movies and music.  The printer is on the network as well.  The Trane box is an old version of the building automation stuff I work with.  That one was a leftover from somewhere, now it does a few things for my house.

I also have a PoE cable running out to my wireless AP which works much better in a different location.

---

### Post by Skye on 2007-01-08
My server, and the majority of my network hardware, lives in my basement on (or under) the "pantry overflow" table (as you can see by the bottle of Gatorade and the boxes of Annie's Mac & Cheese.)  From bottom to top, there is:

-My fileserver, which I just upgraded to Dapper from Breezy last night.  It features a Pentium II @ 300 MHz, 128 MB of ram, and a 160 gig IDE HDD.  It doesn't do anything more intense than share music and files to my LAN, so it's get plenty of power- and considering it was 20 dollars at the MIT Swapfest, I'm not complaining.
-My IPCop firewall, which is running off an old dell laptop with a broken screen- it runs surprisingly well, considering how beat up the lappy was when I got it off my boss. It also runs an openvpn vpn server, which allows me to bypass the site filter they have set up at school.
-A Netgear 5 port 10/100 switch
-Cable modem (die, comcast, die)
-The hardwired port providing ethernet for the rest of the house- one of those wires runs to the attic, where there's another Netgear switch, a wireless AP, and another set of hardwired ethernet ports for all the upstairs rooms.

I set most of the infrastructure up when I was 12, and it's served me well ever since.

### Post by handy on 2007-01-09
Cool Cambo', some of those parts look familiar! :) 

I've posted a few shots of my server, w/station, general office mess, just for the fun of it!

The big ugly tower is an old file server from an accountants firm whose business I was lucky enough to do a total office hardware upgrade on.  I got to keep the replaced computers & peripherals, & this particular AT case I converted to ATX & have been using for years now, with a variety of different contents.  It has heat pipe cooling on the AMD 64/3500 cpu, & on the 6800 GT graphics card, the main noise comes from the 2 x 35gig, 10,000rpm raptors, to a lesser degree the 80gig 7200rpm maxtor boot drive & any others that may be in the drive draws (unusual these days).  

NOISE!  :(  

I'd be interested in any quiet hard drive mounting solutions that anyone has found?  I'm thinking of building a wooden storage box for them...

Sorry Cameron, I'm not trying to derail your interesting thread. :)

The 2nd machine is used for testing different distro's when one takes my fancy.  Great for reading a how-to post, whilst doing it on the other machine, or visa versa.

All good fun... :)

[Edit:] I just noticed the Adam's Family / Munster's, cobwebs in my room, via the pictures, lol, you can only see them with a flash! :-)

### Post by kvonb on 2007-01-09
OK, here is Zen, he lives in the garage (because of noise and heat) and chugs along 24/7 storing all our downloads and giving us Internet.

Sorry about the blurry photos, my wife keeps dropping the digital camera!

Just about EVERY capacitor has been replaced on this old P4VMM2 mainboard, they are renown for dodgy caps!  Note the bodge jobs on the odd sized caps, and the parallel "tree" arrangement of 3x1200ufs when I couldn't find any suitable replacements.

It actually works like a charm, and is incredibly stable.  You just have to be careful not to move them too much while it's turned on :rolleyes:.

EDIT:  handy - we used to sell those cases, they are VERY sturdy, the only problem being the very heavy and cumbersome one piece lid which I see you have removed :)

### Post by Randomskk on 2007-01-14
I use my servers for a lot of things:
1) hosting my personal site(s), randomskk.net randomskk.com and a few others
2) hosting some friend's sites
3) Jabber server for IM (talk to gTalk users)
4) IRC server for some friends
5) email server for my websites
6) backup server, ie file storage

Now and again I find other fun uses too.

### Post by AusIV4 on 2007-01-14
This is what I call my server. It's really more of a media center, but it serves a number of server purposes such as samba and nfs file sharing, and runs a minimal webserver. I use it for MythTV, playing music, and note the Gamecube next to it, I also use it for playing console games with tvtime.

Specs:
512 MB RAM (I'd add another stick, but for some reason my motherboard won't recognize it)
Intel Celeron D 2.93 Ghz processor
400 GB software RAID
Savage S3 Graphics
Plextor ConvertX TV-402U (Primary TV tuner)
Sabrent TV-FM tuner (Secondary TV tuner, mainly used for gaming)

The thing I like to brag about the most with regard to this machine is the price. I got the case, motherboard, power supply, CPU, fan and 512 MB RAM for $120 after rebate on tigerdirect (the rebate was a bit of a hassle, but I got it). I had 160 GB of disk space, the sabrent tuner and the graphics card from an old computer, the rest I've added since I built it. I replaced the fan that came bundled with it, and took some random piece off of the case because they were noisy, which sucks for a dorm room. All told I've put less than $600 into this machine, and it's as nice as some machines I've seen people pay well over a thousand for.

I'd take it apart and show it's innards, but I'm trying to see how much uptime I can get, and I don't want to take it apart while it's on.

[IMG]http://personal.utulsa.edu/~warren-roberts/Dorm/computer.jpg[/IMG]

### Post by kvonb on 2007-01-15
> All told I've put less than $600 into this machine, and it's as nice as some machines I've seen people pay well over a thousand for.

$600!!   And that would be US dollars.....mamamia!

My server cost:
CPU: P4-1.6 - $40 from 2nd hand computer shop
40 gig laptop hdd for the OS - free, had bad sectors, fixed.
200g hdd for file storage - $129 new
Mainboard - free, was to be thrown out, I fixed it (see the pics) 
the rest is made up of salvaged/repaired/parts lying around the workshop.
Total: $169


My main system cost the most: 

CPU: P4 3.2 Prescott - free from an upgrade I did (long story!)
Mainboard: $65 from ebay
80 gig hdd - free, has bad sectors at start of drive, but works well
1 gig RAM $70
Nvidia 6600gt video card $180 from ebay (xmas present from wife)
Sony G500 21" screen - free from salvage pile at 2nd hand computer shop - fixed
DVD burner: $95
All the rest is made from stuff lying around the workshop.
Total: $410

Oh and I also get 40 gigs/month free on my 512/256 link as I am a re-seller for their service 8).

### Post by RandomJoe on 2007-01-15
> **Titi said:**
> huh, why do you all have servers? am i the only one around here that just has a computer, nothing more? i don't even think i know anyone with his own server. really, what's it for?
There are all kinds of things one can do with a server...  or two...  (three?!? :mrgreen: )

At the moment, my server has Apache running for me to play around with, houses a 1TB RAID5 array that I store all my movies and music on so I can watch/listen from any computer in the house (or even outside the house via wireless), monitors my network cameras with ZoneMinder, and lets me connect in from the Internet via SSH or OpenVPN.  I also back up all my other computers to it.

I also used to have a MythTV server in there (before ditching cable) so it could record shows whenever they were on.  I'm thinking about reconstructing that, as I now have a digital TV tuner card for over-the-air reception.

The nicest part to me is I can have smaller/lighter/quieter machines where I'm actually at (notably the one connected to the projector and stereo in the living room) while a higher-horsepower server does all the Real work in the back room without annoying me with noise/heat/etc.  (Granted, my new Core 2 Duo desktop system blows this out of the water - it's cooler, quieter and FAR more powerful than anything else I have! :rolleyes: )

This brings to mind the next question - why have so many _other_ computers? -- I have a desktop system that I sit at most of the time, with three screens - LOVE being able to spread things out.  But it's quite immobile, and needs a big desk!  Then there's the laptop for "whenever/wherever" especially on warm spring/summer evenings outside.  The third "regular" is the PC that runs my projector system.

But yes, I could actually do everything I do with computers on just a single machine!  I just wouldn't enjoy it very much...! 8)

---

### Post by xmastree on 2007-01-29
**Great thread!**

Right, here's some pics of a server I made for my Internet Cafe. It's actually quite a decent machine, Athlon 2400, 1Gig, GeForce4, but in a very old desktop case.

**A sleeper**.

You can just make out the hacked bluetooth dongle above the floppy, stuck there with epoxy. Hacked so that I could fit a better light, to shine through the front panel.

(yes, that's the rubber grip from an old pen.)

### Post by AvWijk on 2007-02-18
My &#8364; 0-, server , animated :) 

[IMG]http://homepages.fcj.hu.nl/1504286/images/briopc.gif[/IMG]

I've got it for free, it originaly was a Celeron 433 with 64 MB and Win 98, upgraded as much as possible. It completely runs with free software AND hardware :P

Specs are:

Celeron 533 Mhz
256 MB ram
80 GB harddisk
Dual Intel 10/100 Nic

It's small-cased and very silent (most important feature) and does it job very well and fast, with Ubuntu 6.06 LAMP and Apache, PHP, MySQL, Samba, Hamachi. Too bad I cannot upgrade the CPU any further, a limit of the mainboard I think (its a HP Brio D75xx) But for now its fast enough, the performance it just outstanding for what it needs to do. Win2k3 server with the same services is 10 times slower on a hardware configuration 10 times faster.

### Post by Aberrix on 2007-02-20
Just finished wiring my house with Cat5e. I moved my server to my new 'network rack' so I thought I'd show it off :)

[img]http://www.leveleight.org/gallery/5220-2/DSC02086.JPG[/img]

On top is my networking gear;
Metal network cabinet
Linksys WCG200 (Cable Modem / Router / WAP)
Dell PowerConnect 3248 Switch
Patch panel
UPS

(I didn't feel like trying to mount the network cabinet on the wall, so I just built a shelf. I like it better actually as it allows me to have some towers below and some storage)

On the bottom are my server(s), the server on the left is as follows:

Ubuntu 6.06 LTS Server, The Perfect Setup w/ ISP Config.
- Apache Web server (SSL-capable)
- Mail server (with SMTP-AUTH and TLS!)
- DNS server
- FTP server
- MySQL server
- POP3/IMAP
- Quota
- Firewall
- Samba
- etc

All running off an old Dell Optiplex GX1 I got for **FREE** from work.
PIII 500Mhz
512Mb Ram
80Gb HD
300Gb HD
Ubuntu Stickers! :)

The server on the right is currently decommissioned until I refurb it with a new heatsink, case fans, hopefully upgrade to 1Gb of RAM and also hopefully a new HD, possibly RAID but it is as follows;
AMD Thunderbird 1.3Ghz
768Mb Ram
40Gb HD

Future plans are to migrate everything over to the 1.3Ghz box (eventually) and then turn the Dell GX1 into a NAS (ie: FreeNAS) :)

### Post by hkgonra on 2007-02-22

Agreed, you can use any one of your pc's as a central repo. 
You can buy seperate print server for each printer. 
You could run backups from one to another. 
You don't even need your own server to host a website, there are MANY places out there that will host your website for free. 

There are many different ways to do things. 
I have tried several but I like the idea of having one dedicated server that is Raided to hold everything. 

Plus a server , like most of what we all seem to do, is just another toy to play with.

### Post by hkgonra on 2007-02-22
> **Mateo said:**
> Why do you need a print server at all?  Plug your printers up directly to your router.  That's what I do, with 2 printers, works on ever computer.

### Post by hkgonra on 2007-02-22
> **Mateo said:**
> most printers today have ethernet cards.  If you have an old printer that's true, they don't, but if you're going to spend the money to build a print server, why not just spend it on a new printer ;)


:confused: 
It may be different where you are but other than a very few printers I have seen is stores which cost over $500 I have never been in a store and seen a printer with an ethernet card. 
I know a very few exist under that price but they are not something you will see in a Best Buy or comporable store. 
Now if you are talking about high-end laser printers then obviously most have ethernet cards but I have never seen anyone purchase one of those for home use.

As far as the cost of building a print server ( or full fledged home server for that matter ) hardware that would fit that bill is readily available ( at least where I live ) for free, and we all know that the software is free. ;)

---

### Post by tomane on 2007-02-22
> **Mateo said:**
> most printers today have ethernet cards.  If you have an old printer that's true, they don't, but if you're going to spend the money to build a print server, why not just spend it on a new printer ;)
Unfortunatelly, that's not true... Networking capable printers are still rare, although we're making progress, and more expensive than the networkless equivalent. I'm refering to laser printers, btw. If you look to the inkjet territory, things get even worse, unless you're willing to pay a lot more for your printer, just to get an aditional 20€ or less worth of electronic components ;).
Well, at least that's how it is where I live.

As for the extra money for the print server, you are right, but usually, and this thread actually confirms it, server hardware is salvaged material that you get almost for free, so it probably is cheaper than the extra money for a networked printer *and* you have the ability to have a centralized repo for miscelaneous files, not to mention a new toy :lolflag: :D

€0,02
cheers,
--to

### Post by RandomJoe on 2007-02-22
> **jethro10 said:**
> Can someone expplain to me why I need a server/network at home.
Aside from filling some useful functions that could admittedly be handled reasonably well in other ways, the most compelling reason for me is:

[SIZE="5"]**Because I Can!**[/SIZE] :guitar:

Fiddling with networks is my hobby.  If I could go out and find a netadmin or sysadmin job that assured me I wouldn't ever have to fix a Windows box again, I'd do it in a heartbeat.  Until then, I satisfy myself running a fancier network in my home than many businesses have! :lolflag: 

Seriously...  I just started a new job, and I've once again become the sorta-kinda sysadmin because no one else has a clue.  (My primary job has little to do with office networks - I do building automation systems.)  I walked into an office of ~25 machines, a "file server" that was a network-attached USB hard drive (!!!), a 16-port 10/100 switch.  (They have some small switches scattered around on desks too!)  The 'net connection was a Cisco 1400 (think that's right) giving them only 25 IPs, no DHCP.  No external access from their remote office.

Now, a week later, I have replaced the Cisco with a Linux firewall/DHCP/DNS/VPN server (just like at home) and the USB drive has (just in time - the drive bearings are going out!) been replaced with a proper server w/ RAID storage and backups.  Running Linux, using Samba!  As a bonus, the Cisco for some reason was only allowing ~3Mbps inbound.  The Linux box gives us the full 7Mbps connection speed.  Nothing like doubling Inet performance first week in the office! :)

And all thanks to playing around at home...

---

### Post by go_beep_yourself on 2007-10-24
> **mysticrider92 said:**
> Just wondering, why did you use an SLi mobo for a server? They don´t even need a video card or screen when set up right... And n3tfury is right, the pics should be resized or linked to.

Because it functions as more than a server. It's an ingame server, not a dedicated one. That computer is called the Linux beast. It has an 8800 gts 320 mb ddr3 vram pci express 16x card, 2 gb gskill ddr dual channel memory, overclocked amd 3800+ x2 dual core cpu at 2.4 ghz, 2 sata2 320 gb/s drives in linux software raid, 2 dual layer dvd burners, 700 watt 36 amps FSP power supply unit and plenty of cooling. Also, I took the floppy drive out and beat it with a hammer because it is useless and archaic.

### Post by isecore on 2007-12-18
Well, here comes the dodgiest server so far :)

It's mine, and it's in my home office. Don't mind the dustmites, we (me + gf) have a dog + two cats, so no matter how much you clean it still looks like a circus after a few hours.

It's a Sempron 2500+ with half a gig of RAM and slightly less than 1 terabyte of harddrive (972 gigabytes to be exact). It has several functions, most of them are handling email and serving up homepages (with MySQL and PHP). Currently it's the host for five domains. It also acts as ftp-server and network storage for me and my girlfriends computers, as well as crunching Seti@home with the leftover CPU-resources. Of course it runs SSH as well, and we use that quite frequently when away from home to check email and such. It's connected straight to the 100mbs Internet-connection. OS is Debian Stable (currently that's Etch, but it's been upgraded twice - first OS was Woody, then Sarge, now Etch). It runs 24/7 and the best uptime was about 220 days, but then one of the harddrives died and it had to be shut down for the change. On average the uptime is about 4-5 months.

And as you can see, it's not the prettiest of computers. It's housed in a heavily modified and fubar'ed Aopen HX08 that easily is more than ten years old. Most of the modifications however aren't visible, and I won't turn it off and pick it apart just to show you.

Explanations follow below:

[IMG]http://www.isecore.net/dodgy_server_1[/IMG]
The brown packing-tape is to cover up an old hole I chopped up several years ago. A previous incarnation of the machine had a very weak powersupply, and I added a secondary powersupply to keep the harddrives happy. However, when I upgraded it was no longer needed, so I taped the hole shut and used some cardboard for noise-dampening :) (the black cable snaking over the machine is the charger for my Nintendo DS)

The writing on the side is from about four years ago when me and a friend were somewhat inebriated and celebratory. The round sketch is from when I was planning some additional cooling, until I realized I had it all upside-down. The fans that are bolted on is the result of that additional cooling.

[IMG]http://www.isecore.net/dodgy_server_2[/IMG]
There's four harddrives being cooled by the Coolermaster-thingamajig there. Originally designed for the Stacker-cases, I bought one and squeezed it in after some minor modifications. It looks like the fans aren't turning, but I just took the pictures with a very quick exposure.

The holes in the front is for another fan. I quickly drilled them one night a few years ago. That fan is no longer in use, and I'm thinking of instead cutting up the faceplate and adding two large 120mm fans to cool the entire machine instead. The two 80mm fans are dying, they were old even before they started working here, so far they've been running for more than four years straight (with small periods of downtime when I moved house or when the power got turned off).

The powerbutton up at the top of the case is nonfunctional. It was connected to an old AT-powersupply and is useless. Instead I routed the powerswitch to the former reset-button, located underneat the drive-cage. The two LED-lights were added to show activity from the additional IDE-adapters inside the computer, but they were mostly annoying so I removed the cables. The lights themselves are however glued in place, so no removal there!

---

### Post by isecore on 2008-01-27
Here's an update of my server. Recently I bought a new case for my desktop, and thus the server would be upgraded to that one. It's the same type of case, an Aopen HX08 - albeit of a newer revision with some improvements.

The biggest difference though is that this one isn't falling apart from being so heavily modified. This one actually is really nice for a server - loads of space, and with my added cooling in the side it's not only very quiet but also very cool inside. CPU temp is around 28 degrees, not bad!

Plus, it doesn't have crap scrawled all over it. I also added another 512 megs of RAM to keep it happy, and moved it to a less trafficked location in the apartment - people were bumping into it and stuff. The keyboard and TFT will be removed once I verify that it's running stable.

Otherwise, like I said, it's the same computer as in my first post here.

[IMG]http://www.isecore.net/newservercase.jpg[/IMG]

### Post by F1y3r3 on 2008-07-22
> **ghindo said:**
> For those with GUI-less servers:  how do you do things like monitor CPU temperature, assess free disk space, bring up processor information, etc.?  I just set up a server (pictures later), and am still new to this whole "no GUI" thing. :plm_sensors for CPU temperature, df -h for disk space and cat /proc/cpuinfo for CPU info.

### Post by OttifantSir on 2008-07-29
After seeing some of what is out there that normal people use (I thought many of the setups I've seen so far only belonged in dedicated computer centers at large corporations), I've been dialed down a notch.

Anyways, here is the setup in my bedroom (links to Flickr):

[Overview]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/8913510@N02/2713694299/")
[Printers]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/8913510@N02/2713693647/in/photostream/")
[Spare Parts]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/8913510@N02/2713692959/in/photostream/")
[Desktop]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/8913510@N02/2713692369/in/photostream/")
[Server]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/8913510@N02/2714503696/in/photostream/")

Specs: 21" CRT, 15" LCD
Canon Pixma MP520 all-in-one inkjet
OKI B4350 b/w laser
A few drives and other loose change
Desktop: P3 1.23 GHZ
512 MB RAM
DVD-burner
floppy
2 USB1.1
40 GB HDD
10/100 Ethernet

Server: Pentium D2C 3GHz
3GB RAM
DVD-RAM
9 USB2
3.25 TB (not TiB)
Gigabit Ethernet

The desktop is the one machine I don't mess around with. I keep it for online banking and purchasing, reading e-mail and office work. The server still has a few glitches, but mostly work like it should. I also have a ThermalTake Lanbox Lite with Pentium D2C 2.67GHz, 2GB RAM, DVD+RW, 6 USB2, 1TB (not TiB), Gigabit Ethernet, Cinergy TerraTec C PCI DVB-C, HIS Radeon PowerColor 2400 256MB and Gyration Go 2.4 Compact sitting in my living room.

Add a Dell Inspiron 9400 (E1750), and that's all the machines I have at the present. I have a case from a Dell PowerEdge 500SC that will soon be operational again too, but that's for another day and another time.

All this setup really do at the moment is host all my movies, TV-shows, music, pictures and documents. All are connected to the server with NFS, so even the desktop thinks it has apx 3 TB of diskspace (3 1TB WD Caviar GP in LVM on the server)

My dream is to have connectivity all throughout my apartment and to (sometime) set up a VPN-connection so that my family and select friends may use my "database" of movies, shows and music, and I can "take it with me" wherever I go that has a broadband connection.

All of this is running Ubuntu 8.04 Desktop. (Couldn't figure out the Server edition)

### Post by isecore on 2008-07-29
> **ghindo said:**
> For those with GUI-less servers:  how do you do things like monitor CPU temperature, assess free disk space, bring up processor information, etc.?  I just set up a server (pictures later), and am still new to this whole "no GUI" thing. :p

Munin is a quite handy tool to monitor servers. Outputs results from various things in nice graphs you can view with a web-browser. 

Webmin is another handy thing to administer a server. Provides a nice web-interface for most things. Very powerful! Be careful about allowing access to it.

### Post by isecore on 2008-07-29
> **artir said:**
> Why do you need a server @ home. Web hosting is not very expensive.

One word: control.

No one can tell me what I can or cannot do with my server. Sure, hosting is "cheap" provided you put up with some lame shared hosting where you're severely limited by what the provider decides you need.

I can setup as many databases and domains as I want, limited only by CPU and memory. Both of those are very cheap today. I can host my friends sites, I can host email.

And that's the second thing, there's no limit to what I do with it. Sure, I can host websites. I can host an FTP, an image-upload. Whatever happens to be my hearts desire. But I can also setup a local SAMBA-share, manage network sharing - whatever I need.

---

### Post by Delever on 2008-07-29
> **artir said:**
> Why do you need a server @ home. Web hosting is not very expensive.

Development, giving others to test, changing anything easily, total control anytime, one person to blame for failures.

> Why do you need a server @ home. Web hosting is not very expensive.
Because it is. I have 20GB of Email space, unlimited MySQL databases, 20GB of web space, and all the bandwidth my non-limiting ISP can give me. This would cost *boatloads* if I had purchased it. Plus, all the other services running on my box, like my printing server, custom-built instant messaging server, and all sorts of other goodies. All while running a Hardy desktop with C-F.

I've had people utterly bewildered at the speed of my site who refuse to believe it's running on a basic consumer high speed package.

### Post by OttifantSir on 2008-07-30
> **artir said:**
> Why do you need a server @ home. Web hosting is not very expensive.

Web hosting means giving control over your content to someone else.

With my content, numbering in at about 2.5TB, uploading that to a web hosting service would take around a month JUST to upload, if I could afford to pay indefinitely for that amount of space on a web host. Most web hosting services I have seen also have a datalimiter, requiring you to pay more the more content and traffic you have. And when I would want to access it, it would require connecting to some website and download it AGAIN. And what would happen if I were to forget to pay? Or if I couldn't afford to pay? My content would be wiped. 

For a family it makes even more sense. You spend the big money on ONE machine that everyone can access, and purchase cheap machines to run as thin-/fat-clients. You can actually save money by using a server, giving each member of a family their own computer where they can do things for themselves, all the while ensuring that whatever content you have is safe should you FUBAR.

---

### Post by irv on 2008-08-01
> **ghindo said:**
> Good GOD I want to have your ISP.  Where do you live and who is your ISP?  What do you run on your server?
I am in a very small town 2500. Back in the 80's a small company started up in Winona MN (35 miles from me) call Hiawatha Broad Band, now called HBCI. It started with dial-up, but within the last couple of years they installed fiber in our small town and can now offer TV, Phone, and Internet all on this fiber. Normal the Internet speed is 3MB for $33 if you have all 3 service. I told them I would pay the extra ten bucks for 4MB, but they told me they could only give me 5MB for that price, so I took it.About 6 months to a year ago I started checking my speeds, and it has been going up until it is where it is now. I don't know what happen, but I am not complaining.
I have a web server, but I only use it for my files I want to share with the world. I do not host webpages. I also have a web business but I use a hosting services who service up the pages. When I am travel around, I can get to all my files on this server if I need something. Even when I was in Africa and Europe I could get to them.

### Post by Old_Grey_Wolf on 2008-08-16
**> **artir said:**
> Why do you need a server @ home. Web hosting is not very expensive.**

There was a problem at my job that the software developers identified as as lack of communication. Someone suggested a message board to enable cross development team communication. I listened to the suggestion, and tried it out by installing a LAMP stack on one of my computers at home. I told my family about the experiment. They began setting up forums, blogs, PMing each other, and so on. I decided to add a print server, file server, streaming audio server, etc. 

[B]It actually made it easier to maintain my network of family computers on my LAN running Windows XP, Vista, and Ubuntu.

It is free, completely private, and I don't have to worry about my children putting a copyrighted music files on the server. It is not exposed to the Internet.[/B]

---

### Post by whitegourd on 2009-03-18
> **Dragonbite said:**
> Imagine cooling is pretty easy with that setup!  Just don't be looking at it while you're drinking soda and somebody tells you a good joke! Spewing soda all over it will mess it up reeeeeal fast!

Haha. I sure hope that won't happen!  I tried adding a fanless heatsink from a D201GLY2 board (it got zapped last year using the wrong power supply brick).  The heat from the northbridge went up to 61c w/ load.  So for now the only moving parts are the northbridge heatsink fan and the hard drive.

This D945GCLF board, 1GB memory, and the PICO PSU 90, were the only things I needed to get the little project completed, the rest I had laying around the house.  I'm so happy that it fits on a regular clipboard, saves a lot of space and is pretty silent.

### Post by isecore on 2009-03-20
> **sujoy said:**
> love this thread. :D

keep 'em coming guys. i dont have a server yet, but i plan on setting one up when i earn enough to buy one ;)

The big cost is electricity - at least if you're gonna run it 24/7 as a dedicated server. I think the money I've spent on hardware is a fraction of what I've paid for power since 2003 when I launched it.

In fact, when I started the machine was a lowly Pentium 150 Mhz. It's just grown over the years. But again - electricity has been by far the biggest cost for me.

### Post by Dragonbite on 2009-03-20
> **ghindo said:**
> There are a lot of ways you can work around that, though, undervolting your server, running lightweight applications, etc.

---

### Post by isecore on 2009-03-20
> **ghindo said:**
> There are a lot of ways you can work around that, though, undervolting your server, running lightweight applications, etc.

Although technically that's alleviating it, not working around it. Unless you slap up your own solar/wind-power on the roof :)

I can't do this. I host seven domains, complete with PHP, MySQL and various other stuff. They're all fairly well-visited. SpamAssassin sorts through maybe 30k spam-email per day.

I simply can't handle this on a lower-end processor than I already run (Sempron 2500+) and I've already removed a majority of the drives in the machine to make it less power-hungry (went from fifteen drives to four).

So, it's all relative :)

### Post by alex2399 on 2009-03-23
I don't have a server, but I would like to ask something.

Seeing most of these setups, the biggest scare for me is that it would catch fire some day, a failing and overheating fan due to blocking, melting of capacitors/transformers/coils/resistors in the PSU, all that dust just waiting to get burned.
Have personally witnessed seeing electronics go up in smoke, part because at a time it was my job working with electronics(FYI, fixing/calibrating them, not intentionally creating a ball of fire). But I have also seen household appliances dying with lots of smoke and burned circuit boards. One case I vividly remember was a computer monitor. One day a lot of smoke is coming out of it and quickly turned of. Then opened it up, and where there once probably was a transistor or voltage regulator now was a big hole in the circuit board, and burned all around. Wouldn't like to know what would have happened if I wasn't there at the moment. Have seen enough electric fireworks to make me weary of what bad design can cause. 

So what do you do to minimize the risk of fire? Do you use a smoke alarm, sprinklers, do you tightly monitor temperatures/fans, clean regularly? If you can illustrate your fire-hazard minimizing techniques of your servers, pictures would be nice ;)

I myself clean the inner life of all aplliances regularly when they are out of warranty and avoid putting any appliance on standby so I turn almost everything off when I go to sleep, but since your servers are running probaly 24/7, do you ever think about these dangers?

---

Edit: On the question on fire protection: I hope nothing goes wrong...

### Post by isecore on 2009-03-24
> **alex2399 said:**
> I don't have a server, but I would like to ask something.

Seeing most of these setups, the biggest scare for me is that it would catch fire some day, a failing and overheating fan due to blocking, melting of capacitors/transformers/coils/resistors in the PSU, all that dust just waiting to get burned.
Have personally witnessed seeing electronics go up in smoke, part because at a time it was my job working with electronics(FYI, fixing/calibrating them, not intentionally creating a ball of fire). But I have also seen household appliances dying with lots of smoke and burned circuit boards. One case I vividly remember was a computer monitor. One day a lot of smoke is coming out of it and quickly turned of. Then opened it up, and where there once probably was a transistor or voltage regulator now was a big hole in the circuit board, and burned all around. Wouldn't like to know what would have happened if I wasn't there at the moment. Have seen enough electric fireworks to make me weary of what bad design can cause. 

So what do you do to minimize the risk of fire? Do you use a smoke alarm, sprinklers, do you tightly monitor temperatures/fans, clean regularly? If you can illustrate your fire-hazard minimizing techniques of your servers, pictures would be nice ;)

I myself clean the inner life of all aplliances regularly when they are out of warranty and avoid putting any appliance on standby so I turn almost everything off when I go to sleep, but since your servers are running probaly 24/7, do you ever think about these dangers?

Well, after reading your post my reply might seem filled with danger :)

I rarely think of this. My server is inside my hallway storage room which is fairly well ventilated, although that's simply a coincidence and nothing I gave any consideration.

Most of the components are past their warranty and only occasionally do I blow dust out of the server - usually this coincides with whenever I replace any hardware in it, which is rare these days.

I never turn it off. The only times it gets shut down is either when the power goes off (since I lack a UPS for it) and that is at most once a year. The only other time is when I shut it off for maintenance or such, and that never happens unless there's good reason. I generally leave it turned on even when I go off and travel. Only thing I do is leave the door to the closet open when I go, for ventilation.

Generally speaking I rarely pay much thought to my server. It sits in there, drinking electricity and providing services but as a physical machine I don't think much about it. I of course keep close track of the software and services running, but not the hardware.

---

I also keep a careful eye on temps and dust levels.

### Post by eatont9999 on 2009-03-24
I think if any of my machines were to catch fire, they would sit and burn inside their steel cases. I don't keep many flammable things around them. Not beacuse I am worried about them burning, but because I can't recall any of them being near something.

I have seen many e-machines where the PSU fails and burns a hole through the southbridge chipset. It is funny to see, but the user needs to buy a new PC; and hopefully not another e-machines.

---

### Post by irv on 2009-03-24
My wife makes me keep my server in my furnace room which is separate from the rest of the house. It too is the coolest place to keep it. It is all block and cement floor. I check it on and off because I do updates on it all the time. When it comes to computer; since the 1980's I have never shut off any of my computer they run 24/7. By doing this I have had less repairs on them. I learn this from work where we did the same. 
Only one time did one over heat on me because the CPU fan went out. But all that happen was the PC shut off. (No fire). I feel safe with them running, I believe one is more apt to have a fire from faulty wiring than from computers. 
I do shut off my monitors but the the PC's stay on.
I know I use more electricity, but that's my choice.
Irv

### Post by gtfourdreams on 2009-03-24
wow. this is an old thread.. but it's staying alive :)

Here’s a list of what goodies I have:

(Top to bottom)
    * IBM RS/6000 Server Rack 42U
    * D-Link 24port 10/100 unmanaged switch
      Uplinks to the Linksys Router and allows all my machines to connect to each other. Its unmanaged, auto-sensing, auto-config, etc.
    * Intel Dual P3 933mhz, 2GB pc133 RAM, Dual 500gb HDDs, 160gb OS HDD
      This server holds a Windows Home server on the 160gb and uses one of the 500gb drives for storage, and the second to back up the first drive. (ie. Software RAID 1 - Mirror) I have some pretty important data on there such as 6+ years of digital images and documents. I also use it to store frequently installed software, updates, music, etc.
    * Intel Dual P3 600mhz, 256MB pc133 RAM, 9.1gb 10k RPM hot-swap SCSI
      With Ubuntu LAMP server installed, this machine is primarily used for web development testing.
    * (Servers are housed in two old Premio Server cases with 6x Hot-Swap bays.)


I recently removed the bottom machine (dual p3 600mhz) and replaced it with a DL380 G3, Dual Xeon 3.06ghz, 2x36gb scsi, unit. I plan to use it for the same functions but a little bit more hardcore. :)

I plan to also either a) consolidate the file server to the new proliant server, or b) setup ubuntu on the file server. WHS has it's features... but my 90 day trial ran out and I don't want to purchase it. :D

EDIT: as for fire hazards, mine sits downstairs in the corner of the basement. It stays nice and cool down here even in the summers.>

### Post by gtfourdreams on 2009-03-25
> **irv said:**
> Where in the world did you pick up this server cabinet for the rack mount servers?

Craigslist. A nice IT guy was giving it away for free. Seriously.

It was destiny, as the rack fit snugly in my 89 'Yota pickup. (Another millimeter and I would've had to take my top off) Brought it home and literally rode it down the stairs into the basement. Darn thing weighs a few hundred pounds at least. It was worth it. :)

Old rackmount chassis units are cheap on craigslist. (Cheaper on ebay if you can find one local.)

OH! BTW, since you're from Wabasha... I picked it up from Brooklyn Park. Keep looking on craigslist if you really want one. And make the trip to the cities!!

Thanks for the info. I am a ex-IT guy (now retired) and we never had a nice rack cabinet like that. All our rack mount stuff was on an open rack in our file server room. I don't have any rack mount computer now, so I would not need one, but I was impressed with your setup. Thanks again for the info.

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2009-05-03
My LAN server (ubuntu 8.04 server edition, running the 2.6.24-19 kernel) is mostly used for hosting printers. I also use it to back up my files on occasion. 

Specs: NEC Ready-series media center PC. 128 MB RAM, 80 GB hard drive (originally 10 GB, but I don't trust old HDDs and I needed more,) Pentium II, Voodoo 3DFX. 


```
~$ ssh max@192.168.1.103

max@server:~$ exit
logout
Connection to 192.168.1.103 closed.

Running FreeNAS, but thinking of changing to an old Xubuntu =]

Only contains 2 fans, one slow moving 80mm in front of the HDD's to bring air across them, and one 50mm on what was once a gaming graphics chipset. ### Post by GCFreak on 2009-06-18
*WARNING LARGE IMAGES (1600x1200)*

Sorry, I know my photos are really dark. It's always dark in my house due to me not bothering to put lights on. =P

Here is my setup. They have a small chunk of my dining room all to themselves.

** see attached images**

[http://gcfreak.sepwich.com/images/computer/](http://gcfreak.sepwich.com/images/computer/) - Older images of the Dell, shows it being put together with the current layout, and shows the internals

The big black machine is a Dell PowerEdge 1600SC, made for small business setups. My particular one has two dual-core 2.4GHz 533MHzFSB Xeons, redundant power supplies, 6 storage drives, one backup drive and a DVD-Multi writer. It also came with two case lock keys for me to use. =) It runs CentOS 5.3 and provides my Linux and Windows machines with a NT-style domain, file storage, backup storage, print services and is a multi-client folding@home contributor at "off-peak" times.

Sitting on top of the machine we have a Dell PowerConnect 2324, a 22-port 100BASE-TX switch with two 1000BASE-T ports. On the top left is a D-Link DSL-504T ADSL2+ router, giving us up to 24Mbps (theoretical maximum) of Internet speed. On the top right is an interesting little PC called the "HP e-pc". The thing is TINY, almost silent (hard drive noise only) and very low power (65W ^_^). It runs Windows Server 2003 R2 and I use it for testing stuff and it runs some services when the main server is not available, and it hosts my mIRC bot.

All that empty space will belong to a m0n0wall computer project that I haven't finished building yet (and I'm having problems getting m0n0wall to connect to my PPPoA DSL router, it just won't work! Help is appreciated), and when it's in there and working, I won't have to run that untidy wire around the front of the computer...

Specifications (HP e-pc)
OS: Windows Server 2003 R2
CPU: Intel Pentium III 1GHz
GPU: Intel Extreme Graphics 2 (1024x768 60Hz@32bpp)
RAM: 256MB PC133
NIC: Intel® PRO/100 VE Connection (100Mbps)
Drives: 20GB Seagate
Removable media: Laptop-size CD reader

Specifications (Dell PowerEdge 1600SC)
OS: CentOS 5.3
CPU: 2x dual-core Intel Xeon 2.40GHz
GPU: ATI Rage XL IGP 8MB (1024x768 60Hz@32bpp)
RAM: 2048MB ECC-registered DDR266/PC2100
NIC: Intel® PRO/1000 MT Connection (1Gbps)
Disk controllers: Dell PERC 3/SC RAID controller (4x 73GB RAID 5 [210GB]) and Adaptec SATA RAID controller (2x 250GB RAID 1 [250GB])
Drives: 2x Western Digital WD2500 (250GB) @ 7,200rpm running in RAID 1, 4x 73GB SCSI drives of Seagate, Maxtor and Fujitsu running in RAID 5
Server Backup: 320GB Western Digital WD3200AAJB
Removable media: 1.44MB floppy disk drive, DVD-RW drive
PSU: Redundant power supplies

### Post by Ian_F on 2009-06-20
My turn ;)

Here's a picture of mine, my kids call it "The Noo-Noo"! 

[[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3360/3642926439_56296ff6cf_m.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3360/3642926439_e89d4a64ee_o.jpg")

Hopefully the reason for the ducting is obvious but if not let me explain. The server lives in a relatively airtight cupboard and the ducting is to allow airflow through the case. I cut a couple of holes in the top of the cupboard and attached those “boxes” to them. The "funnel" on the top of the case covers a 22cm case fan and the ducting is 10cm. This is the best idea I could come up with to get the exhaust air from that fan into the ducting.

Whilst it might all look a bit naff the ducting does work really well. And when the cupboard doors are shut you really wouldn't know it was there.

### Post by handy on 2009-06-20
> **irv said:**
> If it wasn't for all us Linux server users, I wonder how many of these older machines would be in landfills or in some junkyard. I think we are doing our part to keep them running and doing something useful. 
Keep up the good work.

I agree whole heartedly. :)

I haven't been able to get anything useful from our rubbish dump recyclers all year?

Late last year I picked up a Dell Optiplex GX150, PIII 7**Mhz, 256MB RAM, 10GB HDD, for $5-. Which I set up as an IPCop/Copfilter box.

It runs 24/7 its quiet & with the Copfilter add-on I gain superb service from Privoxy & ClamAV (I know I don't need ClamAV) the use of both of these services doesn't slow down my internet speeds, which I find amazing, considering how Privoxy slowed down my workstation when used prior to the installation of the IPCop/Privoxy box, the Privoxy scripts that come with Copfilter really are incredibly well done.

I also still have my converted AT full tower case, which is running an Athlon64/3500+/2GB RAM GeForce 7950GT AGP card, on a Gigabyte GA-K8NS Ultra-939, it has 3 drive drawers & a Pioneer DVD burner.  Because of the drawers this machine gets to do a few jobs, one is to operate as a FreeNAS server & under such circumstances it has a 2GB drive that boots FreeNAS & for storage a WD 1TB GreenPower SATA drive that has a SATA -> PATA converter on it, which took a little modifying of the drawer to be able to fit the drive & adapter in it.

Currently I use FreeNAS to backup important files from my workstation, once backed up I turn it off.

The tower also boots Mint-6-Xfce on an 80GB drive when I need to reference the web whilst my main 24" alu' iMac {Leopard (rarely) Arch/Openbox/xfce4-panel (preferred :))} box needs fixing, or I have other work for it to do.  The tower is also for testing other distro's/BSD's, though I haven't been into that much of late.

I'm after another cheap $5- box from the recyclers to create a permanent FreeNAS box, which I will move the 2GB & 1TB drives into, & set up to be able to use Transmission as a torrent slave solution.  Setting up Transmission in this fashion will be quite tedious, & the hardest thing I will have had to do with a computer in a long time, unfortunately, but once it is done, I will not have to recreate the configuration scripts.

It is the wee hours of the morning here & I'm to bed shortly so I'll leave photo's to a later date. :)

### Post by Ian_F on 2009-06-21
> **mr-woof said:**
> I see a lot of you on here run your own websites from home, how did you get the dns sorted out? Does your isp allow you to host?

You mean if you have a dynamic IP address? If so, you can use something like DynDNS to give you a static hostname.
Or do you mean the ISP blocks port 80? If so, DynDNS can sort that out too.

---

### Post by dmizer on 2009-06-21
> **mr-woof said:**
> I see a lot of you on here run your own websites from home, how did you get the dns sorted out? Does your isp allow you to host?

This is how we sort out the DNS issue: [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/DynamicDNS](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/DynamicDNS)

As for me, I made sure that my provider allowed me to host a site before I signed up. There are ways around this if the ISP blocks port 80, but I wouldn't suggest it, as it's probably in violation of your contract.

### Post by irv on 2009-06-22
Here is how I have a website on my own server. First I got a static IP address from my ISP. I did this many years ago through my business. Then I set my router to this static IP. Here is the status of my router:
[ATTACH]118595[/ATTACH]
I have an account with 1and1 hosting server, and have a DNS routed to my IP address. Here is a screen shot of my DNS settings. You can see that it matches the IP assign to my router. 
[ATTACH]118596[/ATTACH]
I have my router set for the ports I want to open.

### Post by handy on 2009-06-23
> **irv said:**
> Thanks for the advice, I have an old box doing nothing in my furnace Room. Why don't you put a how-to together and I will try it.

I started a thread late last year, that helped me get IPCop working.  The installation & set up is really very quick & easy (20 to 30 minutes) if you know what you need to.  

I didn't know lots of things. 

But I wasn't in a rush, & got great help from the posts of very helpful people in that thread. 

I had no idea about putting a cheap modem/router into bridge mode (turning off the router all together) & then having to set the rotter (an evil model) back up again, which I had to do multiple times as I found my way through, what was basically my own ignorance. ;)

You will see in my first post in the following linked to thread that I mention the Advanced Proxy IPCop add-on.  I found that it would be of no use to me whatsoever, as there is a proxy built into IPCop & I just don't have enough throughput on my LAN for it to ever be used:  

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=998490](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=998490)

Following is link to a page from the above thread which shows my set up, it might be worth a look first up to prime you:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6303994&postcount=29](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6303994&postcount=29)

This was a thread I got going in the old & now unfortunately closed OOST sub-forum, I think you may find some interest & valuable links in there too:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1005192](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1005192)

You will quickly gather that I don't use IPCop the way that you would.  I just use it as a firewall/router/Privoxy/anti-virus box.

IPCop can handle large numbers, like 300+ machines going through it in commercial installations.

I have been using it for about 6 months - 24/7 & it has never done a thing wrong.  I'll probably put it on a MiniITX board in the future or look into using a Sheevaplug, in the interest of using the least amount of electricity as possible.

If after you have a look at that lot you have anything I can help you with, give me a yell.  There is also good help in the nOOST forum linked to in my sig'.

---

I buy DNS service from DynDNS.com. They have free service but only for their own domains. Sure, there are other free alternatives but DynDNS has always been very good to me. Run software on the machine for eventual IP-changes and reboots and everythings good.

### Post by handy on 2009-06-24

Do you use the Copfilter add-on?  It has some great services, it is the only add-on I need, it fits into IPCop like a hand in a glove. :)

Privoxy & ClamAV operate from Copfilter, they work so smoothly in every way, & they don't slow down the internet, which I find astounding, compared to when you run Privoxy on a workstation.  I don't know about ClamAV on Linux as I have never run anti-virus software on a Linux workstation.

Both IPCop & FreeNAS are two most excellent dedicated installations, I can't recommend them highly enough.

### Post by cariboo on 2009-06-28
It depends on what you use it for, I don't serve any web pages, It strictly serves streaming media, and oher files. I've never seen cpu usage go above 25% on the file server, and the mail server spends most of it's time idling at 0%. The mp3 player has never gone above 10% in the 3 days that its been running.

None of them run gui's so they don't have to work very hard, and total investment is only the cost of the hard drives in the file server, the rest have been salvaged from computers that have since been recycled.

As far as performance goes, the file server boots to a login prompt in less than 10 seconds, Can your desktop do that?

The first incarnation of my server was a Pentium running at 150 Mhz with 128 megs of RAM. Ran just fine, even did PHP/MySQL for my then-nascent blog. Sure, it only hosted one domain, which was far from heavily-trafficked but it ran just fine. It also hosted FTP and mail quite nicely.

### Post by leef on 2009-06-28

It currently runs; php, mysql, apache, vnc, ssh, nfs, samba fileshare, samba printer share, cups printer share, torrentflux, flash mp3 player and streams films with wordpress and jwplayer plugin. It's doing well but it's a little slow loading wordpress. So many cool servers in this thread.

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-06-28
What's a server any ways? Any one care to clarify? I know what an online game server is but, what's the purpose of these servers?

---

### Post by red_Marvin on 2009-06-28
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> What's a server any ways? Any one care to clarify? I know what an online game server is but, what's the purpose of these servers?

A server can do many different things, but it usually revolves around serving some sort of content (web pages, files, music, cat macros) over a network, being it local or the internet.
It differs from a workstation in that it is meant to largely hum along by itself with a contstant set of running applications instead of being directly controlled by a user.

---

### Post by dmizer on 2009-06-28
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> What's a server any ways? Any one care to clarify? I know what an online game server is but, what's the purpose of these servers?

A server provides a service (usually network based) to other computers. 

Wiki is a bit more verbose: [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_(computing)](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Server_(computing))

---

I was hoping I could strong ARM one of those things into being an IPCop box, but IPCop needs i386 compatibility, so the ARM processor rules the SheevaPlug out of contention unfortunately.

The following 3 are all worth thinking about though, when it comes to low power usage 24/7 servers like IPCop needs to be:

[http://www.pcengines.ch/alix2d13.htm](http://www.pcengines.ch/alix2d13.htm)

[http://www.soekris.com/net5501.htm](http://www.soekris.com/net5501.htm)

& scroll down the page on this one:

[http://www.tomshardware.com/reviews/Atom-Athlon-Efficient,1997.html](http://www.tomshardware.com/reviews/Atom-Athlon-Efficient,1997.html)

### Post by Zelandeth on 2009-07-03
Well, snapped a photo of my webserver which lives in my wardrobe.  It's an old Duron 1200 which was built entirely out of scrap parts, including a monitor which had a run in two owners ago with a BB gun (I didn't ask!)...but enough of the panel works for what I need it for, which is very rarely if I actually need to poke the BIOS.  If I remember rightly, it's got a 40Gb harddrive and 256Mb of Ram in it at the moment.  Might be a 60Gb HD...can't remember to be honest, was very much a matter of what I had laying around at the time.  Had until I moved lived behind the sofa in our living room, wired directly into the router.  Unfortunately moving required rethinking of that, as the phone socket's inconveniently located in the hallway, and we keep tripping over the router, never mind the server next to it.  So there's not a Cheap'n'Nasty (TM) wireless antenna which sits on top of the box.

[img]http://loz.zelandeth.org/misc/server.jpg[/img]

You can just about see the machine in question buried under the workbench which is buried under other junk.

Runs Hardy, in low graphics mode because it can't figure out what to make of the el-cheapo graphics card from 199something.  It also runs Hardy very slowly - but once it's got itself up and running, it seems to be able to keep up with running a webserver, so it'll do the job.  Would probably run it entirely headless if I was confident to actually do the initial setup and configuration of things from the command line - which I reckon I might actually be in with a chance of now.

Not had uptimes into three digits yet, but have only had one crash in the year or so it's been running, and that was when the power supply expired.  Naturally, when I was on holiday so couldn't fix it for several days.  That irked me, I don't like unnecessary downtime.

I have Mint-6-Xfce in a drive drawer for installation into no.2. machine, when I (rarely) need a web reference machine whilst working on Arch.  

The same machine has a couple of drives in drawers for FreeNAS, 2GB to boot the system & 1TB for storage, I just boot FreeNAS to backup stuff from the iMac which dual boots Leopard & Arch & then shut it down, as the no.2. machine is noisy & thirsty for power. 

Then there is the IPCop/Copfilter firewall/router (& other services) PIII/7**Mhz/256Mb RAM/10GB HDD headless 24/7 box which I'm getting pretty close to replacing with something that will use even less electricity; it will need to boot IPCop from a flash card, & probably be an Atom powered dual onboard network interface job.  (There are lower power usage solutions but they will just cost me so much more initially that they are probably beyond me, time will tell.)  That motherboard will most likely be a MiniITX running a single core Atom, as that is all it will need, & again, it will use less juice than the PIII.

I'm also looking at building a dual core Atom MiniITX FreeNAS box, so that I can make it a headless FreeNAS slave, allowing me to easily add torrents to it from my no.1 desktop machine.  The slave will run 24 hours per day for however many days when it has the need & use less juice than the no.2. box which is still running an Athlon64 - 3500+ with 2GB RAM, & too much GPU.  That thing sucks far too much juice when it has to be working overnight.

Anyway, that's how I am computer wise m8, beyond that isn't really appropriate for forum threads I think. ;)

All the best Cam'.

### Post by Warren Watts on 2009-07-11
Here's my humble setup:

Server:
An ancient 500 Mhz P-III I found in the alley down the street!
Ubuntu 8.04
1 - 15GB PATA HDD 
1 - 120 GB SATA HDD

I use the server primarily for providing network storage (using Samba and NFS) for the family's MP3 library, daughter's ever growing digital picture collection, and for storing various Linux ISOs. (You can NEVER have too many Linux Distros at your fingertips!)

It also serves as an FTP server and as an Apache web server for my own personal uses.

It runs headless; I use SSH for administration purposes and writing PHP and Perl scripts.

I currently have five other computers on the network, one of which is connected wirelessly.

Three of the other computers appear in the picture;  I am short a monitor at the moment, as my wonderful 19" CRT died last week.. :-(

Oh, and please ignore the empty Mt. Dew and potato chip trash under the desk....  I am a slob after all....

---

### Post by Warren Watts on 2009-07-11
> **dragos240 said:**
> I can't ignore 2 xp computers in view..... :lolflag:

I wondered how long it would be before someone commented on that. :grin:

When it comes to my family's day-to-day computing needs, XP just does the job better for us.  The family just isn't big on the whole GNU/Linux OS experience.

The Athlon 64 is dual boot Jaunty/XP Pro, and the server is strictly Ubuntu, but all the other machines in the house are straight XP.

Ubuntu is perfect for the server, however.  "Straight out of the box", a LAMP server install gives you everything you need, already set up and running.  Spend a few hours setting up the features you need (in my case Samba, NFS, FTP, and Apache) and "poof!" instant server.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2009-07-12
Wow, some of those servers are quite impressive hardware... and some are old hardware with an impressive workload.

This is basically a picture of my server:
[IMG]http://www.aywun.com/productimages/MI-100.png[/IMG]

It runs off an SSD (okay, a flash drive poked in the back) and contains a 1TB 3.5 inch hard disk for data. The motherboard has a passive-cooled Intel Atom single-core CPU which works very well for my needs. As far as networking goes, it's hooked straight into an ADSL router, and the router is hooked into Homeplug networking so my desktop can access the network.

The server uses Ubuntu 8.10 with Gnome.

It runs Samba for file sharing and Rhythmbox for DAAP. I also send large video files to it and invoke ffmpeg remotely, so I can encode my DVDs to H.264 overnight without leaving my big power-hungry desktop on.  I also use the 'at' command to tell it to download big files overnight, or Firefox through VNC to have it upload large files to video sharing sites overnight; once again, to save power.

I did used to have torrents downloading and seeding overnight (cron job tells transmission-daemon to go unlimited at 10pm, and at 7am a cron job tells transmission-daemon to limit traffic to 0kbps). But something was going on - I was getting DoS packets sent to me all the time while torrenting, which might have caused my internet connection to go over my ISP's limit. After that I turned off the torrent capability.

I'm very happy with the server. There are only three things I'd change: The power supply (which has a noisy fan), the fact that X won't start without a monitor connected (can this be changed?), and maybe the case - I didn't need such a big case, but it was the only Mini-ITX case I could get at the time that supported 3.5 inch HDDs.

---

### Post by hessiess on 2009-07-19
> 
~What is the best way to share files? I will have all my pictures, documents and music @ server. I will eventually need to see/edit/use these files.

SSHFS

>  
~What do you usually do about playing music? Would you copy the files to the  client and play them, or the sharing speed is fast enough to play them from the server?

play from the mounted SSHFS file system.

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-07-19
Whoa :o When did this come back? :D 

I recently upgraded my old 451Mhz PIII server to a nice PIV 1.7Ghz with 384Mb of DDR RAM. Took the SATA raid card and the two 250Gb drives from the older server (damn IDE =]). Just like the old one, runs FreeNAS, though upgraded to 0.69.2. Acts as a file and ftp server, and once I figure out how to work it properly, it'll do RSync too. 

Boots from a CD, which loads into RAM, and retrieves the config file from a floppy disk =] 

The best thing about this new one though is that the case is much thicker, and the fans are larger, meaning that even in the middle of the night, with 2 80mm fans and the CPU cooler running all at full tilt, with the fan in the PSU too, when I walk 5 feet away from it, I can't hear it =] Which is extremely important, seeing as it lives in my hall, so would wake the whole house. Current uptime is 10days >.<

Yup, in my hall which isn't far from all the bedrooms, its tucked under the hall table, next to the old Win98-DSL computer =] Run's 24/7, so being quiet is important =] 

And the CD to Ram, config from floppy? :D Ya seriously cool I thought =] Means that all the HDD space is availble for the network (even though FreeNAS is <90Mb). And an added bonus, is that seeing as the server isn't accessed too often, after 5 minutes, the harddrives spin down, reducing heat, wear and noise. If the OS was running from the harddrive, it would be able to spin-down. So live booting to RAM suits my needs perfectly =]

As for the JBOD exclosure, looks good =] Are you gonna connect this to a server or just to your main computer? And 4Tb storage? :O Nice! :D 

Im currently working on making a pure backups server, with two 320Gb drives, in RAID, so as to be redundant =]

Well, finally got a TorX screwdriver, and cracked it open, to reveal a gorgeously blackened and burned interior. Completely fried, everything bar the 320Gb harddrive, but thats SCSI, no no use to me :(

### Post by gletob on 2009-07-23
Ok so I now have a server.  I was up at Grandma's for about a week (I wanted to see DC since we got screwed out of all the field trips in elementary school) and she was cleaning stuff up and had and old Emachine that she didn't use.  It's got an AMD K6 333mhz, 160 Mb of DRAM, a 3D ATI Rage IIc (good luck getting that to ever work), CD-ROM, and a 1.4 Mb Floppy.  She runs the LAMP install of Ubuntu Server with Deluge Web UI for torrents, Samba for file storage (and hopefully printing if I find a nice older printer at a yard sale), mt-daap for streaming music, OpenSSH so I can maintain it from anywhere, DynDNS, Webmin for management, and I was running WikiMedia but I removed that after I found I had absolutely no use for it.

It's HDD mounting bracket is missing but it's tucked away in the corner of the room so I'm not concerned about the contacts touching the metal case or anything.

And you'll notice that the heatsink fan is not moving even though the computer was on when I took the pictures.  It was extremly noisy and the temps only went up 5-10 C under heavy load.

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-11-09
> **GreenDance said:**
>  </snip>

Dell GX50 - Ubuntu 9.04 Server
 1.2GHz CPU
 256MB RAM
 20GB HDD

:KS


My school has about a million of those things :) Wish they would give me one though :) Can't complain, they've already given me 6 computers

My main server is now at ```
11:22PM  up 63 days, 18 mins, 2 users, load averages: 0.00, 0.00, 0.00
``` uptime

The other day I downloaded 9.10 Server, burned it, and popped it into an old PIII. I was amazed it booted, and installed, its a 451Mhz PIII with 128Mb PC-100 RAM, a 6+9b IDE HDD, and 2^2Gb flash drives. Its acting as a torrent slave with rTorrent, which works great, loads up torrents placed in a certain dir, and stops seeding when it reaches a certain upload amount. And best of all, the server has yet to go over 28Mb of RAM. Beautiful :) I'm gonna add another 2GB flash drive, and try to get them together in a software RAID, if thats possible

My backup server however is a different story. The fan on the heatsink gave up the ghost, and the CPU (a 2Ghz PIV) was starting to cook itself. So until I can buy another cooler, that's out of action. Just hope that nothing happens my other PCs, my backups are out of date :(

I opened up my main server the other day, something I try not to do unless somethings wrong, I just wanted to check heat levels when its running flat out. Its stays fairly cool, HDDs don't go above ~35C, but idle at 20C, CPU is cold, the CPU fan runs flat out, powered by molex, but is still quiet, its a heavy case. But damn was it dusty in there. So, whilst the server was running, I **VERY** carefully stopped the CPU fan and cleaned the heatsink and case :) Thankfully no static :)

EDIT: Added an older pic of my Torrent Server before I added the second HDD and installed Karmic. The CPU used have a small, **EXTREMELY LOUD** fan, and the GPU still has its one, you can just about see it. That's unplugged now though, it does very little work, and can be cooled by that 80mm fan that I mounted, yes with string, above the heatsink and GPU. Cools the thing pretty well, and much more quiet than with those two little fans

### Post by ShakeyJake on 2010-01-15
I took my server offline today to upgrade the boot drive and I thought I'd finally contribute to this awesome thread. I know it's been dead for a while but I think another resurrection is in order.

Specs:

AMD Athlon 4600+ (With Scythe Shuriken HSF)
Zotac 8200-C-E
4GB OCZ Platinum
Patriot PS100 32GB SSD ( for /)
Western Digital Caviar Green 1.5TB HDD (for /home)
All wrapped up in a Silverstone mini-ITX case with a very quiet and 80% efficiency PSU and a 12cm fan.


It's mine but it's open to the whole flat. As for the people questioning why you'd have a server. Well, in the six months it's been here it has:

Regularly backed up my PC and laptop (not enough room for everyone to do this).
Acted as a massive file dump when people upgrade/reinstall their pcs.
Hosted our very own chat room and internal web page.
Saved my skin when I've forgotten to take work into uni/home with me as I can access it from anywhere.
Been a headless torrent box.
Streamed media to a total of 11 devices including desktops, laptops and xboxs.
Acted as a lightwave render node.
Acted as a central file server for the uni assignments.
Encoded/ripped/transcoded etc etc movies and music overnight.

And I'm sure there are many more things that I've forgotten about.

[IMG]http://i50.tinypic.com/23igk0w.jpg[/IMG]
[IMG]http://i50.tinypic.com/142yph4.jpg[/IMG]
[IMG]http://i50.tinypic.com/9ktuo8.jpg[/IMG]
[IMG]http://i47.tinypic.com/2hf8bqd.jpg[/IMG]

### Post by ShakeyJake on 2010-01-15
@CharlesA

You've got to compromise somewhere. Personally, I wish I'd had more HDD room too. A server without RAID feels borderline criminal to be honest. Having said that, everything that's on there is either not important or backed up elsewhere. 

Most of that machine was originally going to be my desktop, but the board did not support my intended CPU so I filled in the CPU and original boot drive with parts I already had and it became the server. Had I planned a new server from the ground up it would have had more, smaller HDDs in RAID and a lower power CPU. Likely a dual core Atom. By now though a new board will take a long time to pay for itself through slightly lower electricity bills.

Your 'always use the right tool for the right job' sig has got me thinking how not purpose-built that thing is.

---

### Post by GCFreak on 2010-03-05
I've always loved this thread. I don't want it to die, plus its been a while since I've posted my setup, so here it is =)

[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0029.JPG[/img]
Here they are, in all their glory! The left machine is [Dull](http://dickos.dyndns.org/phpsysinfo/index.php?disp=dynamic), a Dell PowerEdge 1600SC with two dual-core Xeon 2.40GHz processors, two 250GB SATA hardware RAID 1, two 80GB SATA hardware RAID 1, two 73GB Ultra320 SCSI hardware RAID 1, running Ubuntu 9.10 Server Edition. She is a web server, mail server, file server, backup server and a multi-client folding@home contributor. The other computer is a custom-built machine with an Athlon 64 3000+ Venice (socket 939) processor, one 80GB SATA system drive, one 200GB backup drive, NVIDIA GeForce FX 5600, running Windows Server 2008. The only reason it runs Windows is because its an AD-DS domain forest master for all the other Windows machines in the house, and it stores backups as well.
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0030.JPG[/img]
A Dell PowerConnect 2324 connects the two servers with the rest of the house, surrounded by spare hardware and a subwoofer (obviously connected to other speakers).
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0031.JPG[/img]
A Dell E151FPb 15" LCD monitor, with keyboard and mouse, connected to a D-Link DKVM-4 4-port KVM switch.
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0032.JPG[/img]
My ventilation =P A common household fan suspended by some planks of wood above an (accidentally created) hole in my wardrobe. I also have a window open all the time in my room to help with airflow.
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0033.JPG[/img]
Left router: Linksys WAG54GP2, provides the ADSL2+ (normally 15Mbps down, almost 1Mbps up) connection and the main WPA2 wireless network. Right router: D-Link DI-524, provides the private MAC-filtered WEP network for my Nintendo DS units to use. Both of which are being held up by supports because they cannot be wall mounted conveniently (have to have longer cables, you see >_>)
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0011.JPG[/img]
[img]http://repos.srb2.org/photo/HNI_0012.JPG[/img]

### Post by handy on 2010-04-03
I've dumped FreeNAS, that I used to run as needed, (drive drawers) due to the excessive power consumption of the Athlon64 3500+ machine that I had available to use.

I now use a small Netgear, ReadyNAS Duo, which apparently uses 4W at idle & 35W when running 2x500GB HDDs. It also runs on a cut down version of Debian, which is nice. A gigabit NIC is incorporated & I can see I'm going to have to get me an 8 port gigabit switch before too long, as it will bring the transfer speeds up into the 20 -> 30 MB/sec range.

I bought it drive-less & put a 1TB WD Green drive in it. It has a browser based interface called Frontview, for config'/observation & an app' called RAIDar, (used for finding any ReadyNAS units on the LAN) for win, OS X, Linux. I'm using Arch & RAIDar wouldn't run on my machine. All I had to do was find out the path to the shares so I could easily set it up to run on NFS.

fsab lines follow :

```
192.168.1.255:/media /mnt/NAS-media nfs  defaults,rsize=32768,wsize=32768,hard,intr,noatime      0       0
192.168.1.255:/backup /mnt/NAS-backup nfs defaults,rsize=32768,wsize=32768,hard,intr,noatime     0       0 
```

On the OS X, side of my machine (which I rarely ever use) the RAIDar software works, & the AFP network protocol & bonjour work just by turning them on in Frontview.

The little black box is quiet, has a small door on the front to access the two hot swappable drives, it has RAID 0 & 1, & another proprietary smart RAID built into the firmware. It doesn't have the ability to do JBOD. 

It can apparently be easily fooled into having the two drives set up as individual RAID-0 which basically gives the same effect as JBOD. This I will do when needed. (I don't like RAID-1, as I consider it to be the quickest way to spread corruption from drive to drive.)

It has the BitTorrent server built in, which can be accessed from a client via a browser interface.  It is a very poor implementation, so thankfully, someone has made a Transmission add-on that is vastly superior. What this means is that you can use the browser interface to give the Transmission add-on torrents to work with & then turn off your computer & go to bed. Thus saving energy/cost & any wear that leaving your computer on may have.

Here is a pretty good hands on type review with an image or two:

[http://brneurosci.org/readynas.html](http://brneurosci.org/readynas.html)

---

### Post by markp1989 on 2010-04-03
the main use for this is as a torrent slave and a htpc, server duties come in 2nd

### Post by jetsam on 2010-05-19
Sorry to ask advice in this lovely thread.  Pics will be delivered eventually...

A couple of honest questions: motherboard transplants... are they ok usually, and does laptop hardware go good in a desktop case?  How long would the operation last?  I'm thinking it's just dremel drill and wood supports and you can do it in about 2 hours if you want to do a decent job...  or take a weekend for a real fine fit, but I wanted to ask the experts before diving in.

---

### Post by The Real Dave on 2010-05-19
> **jetsam said:**
> Sorry to ask advice in this lovely thread.  Pics will be delivered eventually...

A couple of honest questions: motherboard transplants... are they ok usually, and does laptop hardware go good in a desktop case?  How long would the operation last?  I'm thinking it's just dremel drill and wood supports and you can do it in about 2 hours if you want to do a decent job...  or take a weekend for a real fine fit, but I wanted to ask the experts before diving in.

Well, if you mean desktop mobos, ya, swaps usually go fine, so long as it fits in the case ;) Just make sure you have the stands in the right place, and get rid of un-needed ones, so they don't short out.

As for using a laptop mobo in a desktop case, it could probably be done. I'd probably be inclined to suspend it with bungee or something, but if wood's easier for you, go for it. Actually, what I would probably do is just place the whole laptop, case and all, into the desktop case, add on some external harddrives, which could all be stored in the case, and even rig up some case fans in the desktop case to the laptop's power. That though, is probably a lazy way of doing things :)

If you are doing that, make sure to throw up some pics here :)

### Post by dmizer on 2010-05-19
> **CharlesA said:**
> Also, curious what you use for Virtualization.

I was using Vmware Server 2, but I kept having problems with the web only administration interface so I recently migrated to VirtualBox, which allows me to make use of the intel virtualization technology on my CPU. It also gives me better control over my networking so it's much easier to set up and maintain virtual subnets.

I don't care for the RDP based remote access, but it does work and it's sufficient for my purposes.

I was very interested in ESXi, but when I was researching it last I discovered that you needed a Windows machine for the install, or some other essential function.
